<td style="line-height:1.3em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_player" title="Single player">Single player</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multiplayer_video_game" title="Multiplayer video game">multiplayer</a></td>

<p><i><b>Rock Band</b></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Music_video_game" title="Music video game">music video game</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Harmonix" title="Harmonix">Harmonix</a>, published by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Games" title="MTV Games">MTV Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>. It is the first title in the <a href="/wiki/Rock_Band" title="Rock Band"><i>Rock Band</i> series</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> versions were released in the North America on November 20, 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespy-preview_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamespy-preview-3">[3]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> version was released on December 18, 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wii_release_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-wii_release-6">[6]</a></sup> with the Wii version being released on June 22, 2008. The Xbox 360 version was released in Europe on May 23, 2008 while the PlayStation 3, PlayStation 2, and Wii versions were released on September 12, 2008. All four ports of the game were released in Australia on November 7, 2008. The game was to be released in Japan and to be developed by <a href="/wiki/Q_Entertainment" title="Q Entertainment">Q Entertainment</a> but it was canceled.</p>
<p><i>Rock Band</i> allows up to four players to simulate the performance of popular <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock music</a> songs by playing with <a href="/wiki/Game_controller" title="Game controller">controllers</a> modeled after musical instruments. Players can play the <a href="/wiki/Lead_guitar" title="Lead guitar">lead guitar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bass_guitar" title="Bass guitar">bass guitar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drum_kit" title="Drum kit">drums</a> parts to songs with "instrument controllers", as well as sing through a <a href="/wiki/USB" title="USB">USB</a> <a href="/wiki/Microphone" title="Microphone">microphone</a>. Players are scored on their ability to match scrolling musical "<a href="/wiki/Musical_note" title="Musical note">notes</a>" while playing instruments, or by their ability to match the singer's pitch on vocals. Players with the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions can interact with players on the same platform through both online and offline multiplayer capabilities. In addition to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_in_Rock_Band" title="List of songs in Rock Band">58 core songs included on the game disc</a>, over 2,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Complete_list_of_downloadable_songs_for_the_Rock_Band_series" title="Complete list of downloadable songs for the Rock Band series">downloadable songs</a> were released for the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2000th_song_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-2000th_song-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>At launch, the game software was made available in a bundle that packaged it together with the instrument peripherals, as well as for purchase separately. Individual instrument peripherals were released at a later date. The game has received widespread critical acclaim,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> with sales of four million units and global revenues of $600 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-salesfigure_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-salesfigure-9">[9]</a></sup> Players have made over 100 million downloadable song purchases since <i>Rock Band</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-may2011_dlc_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-may2011_dlc-10">[10]</a></sup> The game's success prompted the release of six sequels: <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_2" title="Rock Band 2">Rock Band 2</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles:_Rock_Band" title="The Beatles: Rock Band">The Beatles: Rock Band</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_Rock_Band" title="Lego Rock Band">Lego Rock Band</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Green_Day:_Rock_Band" title="Green Day: Rock Band">Green Day: Rock Band</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_3" title="Rock Band 3">Rock Band 3</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_4" title="Rock Band 4">Rock Band 4</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rock-band-screen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="195" data-file-width="350" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/81/Rock-band-screen.jpg/275px-Rock-band-screen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/81/Rock-band-screen.jpg 1.5x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rock-band-screen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gameplay of a full band playing <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Enter_Sandman" title="Enter Sandman">Enter Sandman</a>". Each instrument is represented by a different interface: bass guitar (right), drums (middle), lead guitar (left), vocals (top). The Band Meter (green meter on left) measures the performance of each band member, while the Energy Meter (gold meter beneath each interface) tracks each player's Overdrive.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Reusing many gameplay elements from the <a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero"><i>Guitar Hero</i> series</a>, <i>Rock Band</i> players use peripherals modeled after musical instruments to simulate the performance of <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock music</a>. Players use these instruments by playing scrolling musical "notes" on-screen in time with the music. <i>Rock Band</i> expands upon the <i>Guitar Hero</i> series, in that it offers gameplay for drums and vocals, in addition to lead and bass guitar.</p>
<p><i>Rock Band'</i>s gameplay and on-screen interface uses a combination of elements from <i>Guitar Hero</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Karaoke_Revolution" title="Karaoke Revolution">Karaoke Revolution</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup> <i>Rock Band</i> has up to three tracks of vertically scrolling colored music notes, one section each for lead guitar, drums, and bass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup> The colored notes on-screen correspond to buttons on the guitar and drum peripherals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup> For lead and bass guitar, players play their notes by holding down colored fret buttons on the guitar peripheral and pushing the controller's strum bar; for drums, players must strike the matching colored drumhead, or step on the pedal to simulate playing bass drum notes. Along the top of the screen is the vocals display, which scrolls horizontally, similar to <i>Karaoke Revolution</i>. The lyrics display beneath green bars, which represent the pitch of the individual vocal elements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup> When singing vocals, the player must sing in <a href="/wiki/Relative_pitch" title="Relative pitch">relative pitch</a> to the original vocals. A pitch indicator displays the singer's accuracy relative to the original pitch. The remainder of the screen is used to display the band's virtual characters as they perform in concert.</p>
<p>During cooperative play as a band, all players earn points towards a common score, though score multipliers and "Overdrive" are tracked separately for each player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup> Overdrive is collected during select portions of a song by successfully playing all white notes within that section (or by using the guitar controller's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tremolo_arm" title="Tremolo arm">whammy bar</a> during white sustained notes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overdrive_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-overdrive-12">[12]</a></sup> Once the Energy Meter is filled halfway, players can deploy their Overdrive, resulting in the "Band Meter" (which tracks how well each player is doing) changing more dramatically. This allows players to strategically use Overdrive to raise the Band Meter and pass portions of a song they otherwise might have failed. Overdrive can be used to activate score multipliers, which vary based on a player's note streak. Players can deploy Overdrive independently of each other, as well as collect additional Overdrive while it is deployed and draining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overdrive_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-overdrive-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each band member can choose the difficulty at which they play (spanning Easy, Medium, Hard, and Expert). If a player does not play well enough and falls to the bottom of the Band Meter, they will fail out of the song and their instrument will be muted from the audio mix. However, any active player can activate their Overdrive to bring failed players back into the song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup> "saving" the band member. However, a band member can only be saved twice; after the third failure, they cannot be brought back for that song. Failed players continuously drag the band's Band Meter down until they are saved. If the player is not saved before the Band Meter reaches the bottom, the band fails the song. Players can earn Overdrive bonuses from "Unison Phrases" and extra points from a "Big Rock Ending."</p>
<p>Unlike the PlayStation 2 and Wii version, players with the Xbox 360 or PlayStation 3 versions can create and customize their own in-game character, complete with adjustable hair, body physique, clothing, <a href="/wiki/Tattoo" title="Tattoo">tattoos</a>, onstage movements, and instruments. Each character is permanently locked into a specific instrument. Using cash earned within the game, the player may purchase items at the in-game "Rock Shop," with which they can customize their rock star. The game features an art maker where players can combine different <a href="/wiki/Clip_art" title="Clip art">clip art</a> elements to create custom face paint, tattoos, clothing designs, instrument artwork, and band logos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-preview_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-ign-preview-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Instrument_peripherals">Instrument peripherals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Instrument peripherals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rockband-guitar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1930" data-file-width="690" height="350" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Rockband-guitar.jpg/125px-Rockband-guitar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Rockband-guitar.jpg/188px-Rockband-guitar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Rockband-guitar.jpg/250px-Rockband-guitar.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rockband-guitar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster" title="Fender Stratocaster">Fender Stratocaster</a> Controller, which features 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frets" title="Frets">frets</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tremolo_arm" title="Tremolo arm">whammy bar</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Effects_unit" title="Effects unit">effects switch</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The game features special <i>Rock Band</i>-branded guitar controllers modeled after the <a href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster" title="Fender Stratocaster">Fender Stratocaster</a> to be used for the lead and bass guitar gameplay. These are similar to the <i>Guitar Hero</i> controllers, as they feature five colored fret buttons on the neck, a strum bar, and a whammy bar. The Stratocaster controller has five additional fret buttons of smaller size located closer to the guitar's main body. These buttons can be used to play notes in guitar solos (denoted by the note track turning blue) as <a href="/wiki/Hammer-on" title="Hammer-on">hammer-ons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pull-off" title="Pull-off">pull-offs</a>, without the need to strum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-6"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup> Additionally, the controller features an effects pickup switch that can toggle between five different effects, which are applied in solos and when Overdrive is activated. Overdrive for guitarists can be deployed by holding the controller in a vertical position or pressing the "Select/Back" button. The controller is offered in both wired and wireless versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-website_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-rb-website-14">[14]</a></sup> Harmonix confirmed most <i>Guitar Hero</i> guitar controllers and additional third-party controllers are compatible with the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-7"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-website_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-rb-website-14">[14]</a></sup> The Stratocaster controller is not compatible with <i>Guitar Hero II</i> or <i>III</i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rockband-drumset.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1840" data-file-width="1610" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Rockband-drumset.jpg/175px-Rockband-drumset.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Rockband-drumset.jpg/263px-Rockband-drumset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Rockband-drumset.jpg/350px-Rockband-drumset.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rockband-drumset.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The drum controller, which features 4 pads, a bass drum pedal, and real drumsticks.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The drum controller features four rubber drum pads and a kick pedal. The pads have colored rings around the edges that correspond to the notes on-screen, representing the <a href="/wiki/Snare_drum" title="Snare drum">snare drum</a> (red), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hi-hat_(instrument)" title="Hi-hat (instrument)">hi-hat</a> (yellow), <a href="/wiki/Tom-tom_drum" title="Tom-tom drum">tom-tom</a> (blue), and <a href="/wiki/Crash_cymbal" title="Crash cymbal">crash cymbal</a> (green). The kick pedal simulates the <a href="/wiki/Bass_drum" title="Bass drum">bass drum</a>, with on-screen notes represented as orange horizontal lines. A pair of authentic <a href="/wiki/Drum_stick" title="Drum stick">drum sticks</a> are included with the controller. Drummers can improvise in special "freestyle <a href="/wiki/Fill_(music)" title="Fill (music)">drum fill</a>" sections of songs, indicated by the columns for each note turning a solid color. Overdrive for drummers can be deployed by hitting the crash cymbal (green note for right-handed configuration) that appears directly after a freestyle drum fill. Harmonix representatives have suggested, "If you can play the drum parts on hard, you can pretty much play the drums [in reality]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-preview_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign-preview-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-website_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-rb-website-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Rock Band</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_Serial_Bus" title="Universal Serial Bus">USB</a> microphone instrument is similar to the model used in the Harmonix-developed <i><a href="/wiki/Karaoke_Revolution" title="Karaoke Revolution">Karaoke Revolution</a></i> games. For the most part, singers are judged on how closely they match the <a href="/wiki/Relative_pitch" title="Relative pitch">relative pitch</a> of the song's vocalist. During "talking parts" that do not judge pitch, a <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phoneme</a> detector will pick up individual vowels and consonants of the spoken lyrics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku-gameinformer_11-8"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku-gameinformer-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gameinformer-preview_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-gameinformer-preview-15">[15]</a></sup> Some sections without vocals will display circle notes, allowing for the microphone to be used as a <a href="/wiki/Tambourine" title="Tambourine">tambourine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cowbell_(instrument)" title="Cowbell (instrument)">cowbell</a> by tapping it or making vocal cues. Overdrive for singers can be deployed by singing in freestyle vocal sections of songs, denoted by yellow artwork in the background of the vocals interface.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Band_World_Tour_mode">Band World Tour mode</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Band World Tour mode">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rockband-band-world-tour.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="183" data-file-width="325" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Rockband-band-world-tour.jpg/225px-Rockband-band-world-tour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/9a/Rockband-band-world-tour.jpg 1.5x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rockband-band-world-tour.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The world map in Band World Tour, which allows the band to select a city, venue, and setlist.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"Band World Tour" is the game's primary multiplayer mode. It allows any combination of 2-4 local players to create a virtual band, play gigs, and tour a virtual representation of the world. Although online play is not supported for Band World Tour, players can use the "Band Quickplay" mode to play together as a band online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bwt-no-online_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-bwt-no-online-16">[16]</a></sup> For the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions of the game, Band World Tour mode lets bands play in 41 different venues spanning 17 cities, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seattle,_Washington" title="Seattle, Washington">Seattle</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts" title="Boston, Massachusetts">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-venue_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-venue-17">[17]</a></sup> After creating their band, characters, and logo, the players can begin playing concerts in small venues in their hometown until they unlock vans, tour buses and private jets, which unlock other cities and continents. Successful performances also earn the band fans, stars, and in-game cash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-worldtour_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-worldtour-18">[18]</a></sup> Most cities and larger venues require the band to achieve a certain number of fans and stars before they are unlocked. In-game venues are inspired by real-life venues and often display local art styles from each of the represented cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-venue_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-venue-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions, rather than complete predetermined lists of songs (like in previous <i>Guitar Hero</i> games), players complete unique sets of activities at each venue. Performances consist of single songs, multiple song sets, "make your own" setlists, and mystery setlists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-worldtour_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-worldtour-18">[18]</a></sup> Players are also faced with decisions that Harmonix refers to as "risk-versus-reward."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-worldtour_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-worldtour-18">[18]</a></sup> For certain performances, bands are faced with an optional challenge that requires the band to average a certain number of stars for their gig in order to reap the rewards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-worldtour_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-worldtour-18">[18]</a></sup> Bands can also choose to perform a benefit concert (earning no in-game money but gaining more fans) or "<a href="/wiki/Selling_out" title="Selling out">sell-out</a>" (earning more in-game money but losing fans).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-worldtour_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-worldtour-18">[18]</a></sup> Additionally, for certain gigs, bands can compete for band personnel, as well as a recording deal with a record label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-worldtour_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-worldtour-18">[18]</a></sup> The "Endless Setlist" provides players with all-day concert experience, as the setlist requires playing the entire game disc's setlist from start to finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scorehero-website-10192007_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-scorehero-website-10192007-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The PlayStation 2 and Wii versions of <i>Rock Band</i> contain a more stripped-down version of the Band World Tour mode, as 2–4 local players will only be able to play by completing predetermined tiers of songs ordered by difficulty. Players cannot create their own characters, nor can they choose a city, venue, or a setlist to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_Tour_modes">Solo Tour modes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Solo Tour modes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Solo Tour" is a single-player mode offered for the lead guitar, drum, and microphone peripherals (there is no support for bass). Rather than feature the open-ended gameplay and features of the next-generation versions of Band World Tour mode, Solo Tour is structured much in the same vein as the career mode in <i>Guitar Hero</i> games. Players choose/create their character (on the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions only) and complete predetermined sets of songs ordered by difficulty, with each instrument's setlist ordered differently. By completing these sets of songs, additional songs are unlocked for play across all game modes. For the PlayStation 3 and Xbox 360 versions, players can use money earned for each performance to purchase merchandise at the "Rock Shop". The character's cash carries over into Band World Tour mode, and vice versa.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_modes">Other modes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Other modes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Players can quickly play any song on any instrument individually in "Solo Quickplay". For a competitive experience, players can individually compete against each other for each instrument type in the "Tug of War" (much like <i>Guitar Hero</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s "Face-off", in which players trade playing sections of a song to move a meter in their favor) and "Score Duel" (much like <i>Guitar Hero II</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s "Pro Face-off", in which each player plays the song in its entirety on the same difficulty level to earn points). These head-to-head modes are available both online (for the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions) and locally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-sept_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ign-sept-21">[21]</a></sup> "Band Quickplay" mode allows bands to quickly play any song; the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions allow any combination of 2–4 local or online players to play as a band, while the PlayStation 2 and Wii versions only supports 2–4 local players. Also included in <i>Rock Band</i> are "Tutorial Mode", which allows players to learn how to play each instrument, and "Practice Mode", which allows players to practice songs for each instrument.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-website_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-rb-website-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtrack">Soundtrack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Soundtrack">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_in_Rock_Band" title="List of songs in Rock Band">List of songs in Rock Band</a></div>
<p>All versions of <i>Rock Band</i> feature the same core 58 playable tracks on the game disc; 45 of these are featured tracks in the main setlist, while the other 13 tracks are "bonus songs" by independent or lesser-known bands, as well as bands made up of Harmonix employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-songlist_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-rb-songlist-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-final-soundtrack_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-final-soundtrack-23">[23]</a></sup> In total, 51 of the 58 songs are master recordings. The Wii version of the game features 5 additional songs. Featured tracks include "<a href="/wiki/Dani_California" title="Dani California">Dani California</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_Chili_Peppers" title="Red Hot Chili Peppers">Red Hot Chili Peppers</a>, "<a href="/wiki/(Don%27t_Fear)_The_Reaper" title="(Don't Fear) The Reaper">(Don't Fear) The Reaper</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Blue_%C3%96yster_Cult" title="Blue Öyster Cult">Blue Öyster Cult</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Enter_Sandman" title="Enter Sandman">Enter Sandman</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Here_It_Goes_Again" title="Here It Goes Again">Here It Goes Again</a>" by <a href="/wiki/OK_Go" title="OK Go">OK Go</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Highway_Star_(song)" title="Highway Star (song)">Highway Star</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Learn_to_Fly" title="Learn to Fly">Learn to Fly</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Suffragette_City" title="Suffragette City">Suffragette City</a>" by <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Wanted_Dead_or_Alive_(Bon_Jovi_song)" title="Wanted Dead or Alive (Bon Jovi song)">Wanted Dead or Alive</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/Won%27t_Get_Fooled_Again" title="Won't Get Fooled Again">Won't Get Fooled Again</a>" by <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a>. All but three songs on the <i>Rock Band</i> disc can be transferred to the user's hard drive on the Xbox 360 or PlayStation 3 to be used for <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_2" title="Rock Band 2">Rock Band 2</a></i>. Furthermore, an extra two songs from <i>Rock Band</i> cannot be carried over into <i>Rock Band 3</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harmonix co-founder Alex Rigopulos commented that the game's soundtrack would be "covering a great breadth, from metal to classic rock to Southern rock to everything in between."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Five <a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">record labels</a> agreed to supply most of the master recordings by their artists for use in the game, including <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> Music, <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Records" title="Hollywood Records">Hollywood Records</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony_BMG" title="Sony BMG">Sony BMG</a> Music Entertainment, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a>'s Universal Music Enterprises, and <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Rhino_Entertainment" title="Rhino Entertainment">Rhino Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downloadable_songs_and_Track_Packs">Downloadable songs and Track Packs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Downloadable songs and Track Packs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rock_Band#Downloadable_songs" title="Rock Band">Downloadable songs for Rock Band series</a></div>
<p>The PlayStation 3 and Xbox 360 versions of the game support downloadable songs. Users can download songs on a track-by-track basis, with many of the tracks digitally bundled together in "song packs" or complete albums at a discounted rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Harmonix has likened the <i>Rock Band</i> game to a new platform for future music releases, and the company built the library of downloadable content up to hundreds of songs within the first year of the game's release by releasing new content on a weekly basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alex-oxm_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-alex-oxm-28">[28]</a></sup> Fifteen songs were made available at the game's launch date. To date, over 1,480 downloadable songs are available<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rock-band-dot-com-dlc_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-rock-band-dot-com-dlc-29">[29]</a></sup> and over 100 million song purchases have been made by players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-may2011_dlc_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-may2011_dlc-10">[10]</a></sup> Downloadable songs are playable within every game mode,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spraynwipe-blog_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-spraynwipe-blog-30">[30]</a></sup> including the Band World Tour career mode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-worldtour_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-worldtour-18">[18]</a></sup> All downloadable songs released before <i>Rock Band 3</i> came out are cross-compatible between <i>Rock Band</i> and <i>Rock Band 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb2dlc_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-rb2dlc-31">[31]</a></sup> Downloadable albums have been a major selling point for the game, with nine albums having been released to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_album_DLC_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-first_album_DLC-32">[32]</a></sup> Currently, most song packs containing three songs are priced at $5.49/440 Microsoft Points, while most individual songs are available for the standard price of $1.99/160 MSP. Occasionally, certain songs are initially priced at $0.99/80 MSP for a limited time. The prices for albums differ, depending on the amount of songs the album contains.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rock_Band_track_packs" title="List of Rock Band track packs">List of Rock Band track packs</a></div>
<p>As both the PlayStation 2 and Wii version lack downloadable content, Harmonix released a series of "Track Pack" standalone games that are sold in retail stores. Each volume contains several of the tracks available as downloadable content for Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3. <i>Track Pack Vol. 2</i> saw an expanded release on the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3, as well. One Track Pack, exclusively featuring the songs of <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a>'s 1991 <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_at_Donington_(AC/DC)" title="Live at Donington (AC/DC)">Live at Donington</a></i> concert, was released in November 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Harmonix Music Systems was previously responsible for making the <a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero"><i>Guitar Hero</i> series</a>, while <a href="/wiki/RedOctane" title="RedOctane">RedOctane</a> manufactured the peripherals and owned the rights to the series. However, in June 2006, RedOctane was bought by <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>, while in September 2006, Harmonix was purchased by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Networks" title="MTV Networks">MTV Networks</a>. As a result of the two purchases, Harmonix would no longer be able to develop future <i>Guitar Hero</i> games. Instead, <a href="/wiki/Neversoft" title="Neversoft">Neversoft</a>, a subsidiary of Activision, would take over development; the company released <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_III:_Legends_of_Rock" title="Guitar Hero III: Legends of Rock">Guitar Hero III: Legends of Rock</a></i> on October 28, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> According to "The Business", <i>Rock Band</i> cost $200 million to develop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Harmonix's Vice President of Product Development, Greg LoPiccolo, stated that the game took about 20 months to develop, already having envisioned the possibility of different instruments before they were completed with the <i>Guitar Hero</i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edge_interview_LoPiccolo_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-edge_interview_LoPiccolo-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In selecting the soundtrack for <i>Rock Band</i>, the developers recognized that they needed to select songs that were recognizable, particularly on vocals; in contrast, when they were selecting songs for <i>Guitar Hero</i>, they were able to pick songs that played better even if they were less recognizable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-av_club_interview_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-av_club_interview-38">[38]</a></sup> They also consider songs that would help players come together socially, such as in The Who's "Won't Get Fooled Again", where they retained the long synthesizer solo such that the band members would all start playing again after it for a big finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-av_club_interview_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-av_club_interview-38">[38]</a></sup> The team were able to introduce songs from smaller artists that they felt were good additions, such as "<a href="/wiki/Maps_(Yeah_Yeah_Yeahs_song)" title="Maps (Yeah Yeah Yeahs song)">Maps</a>" by the <a href="/wiki/Yeah_Yeah_Yeahs" title="Yeah Yeah Yeahs">Yeah Yeah Yeahs</a> and "Electric Version" by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Pornographers" title="New Pornographers">New Pornographers</a> to help also introduce players to those classes of music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-av_club_interview_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-av_club_interview-38">[38]</a></sup> For about half the songs, they hired a studio to sing along to the lyrics as a crowd would at a stadium, such that during the game, when players are performing well, the additional crowd sing-alongs would add to the performance experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-av_club_interview_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-av_club_interview-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Current Harmonix parent company MTV provided financial support to the development process, taking advantage of its stature to facilitate deals with record companies for licensing rights to songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today-39">[39]</a></sup> Several record companies pledged their support by offering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master_recording" title="Master recording">master recordings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joystiq_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joystiq-40">[40]</a></sup> Pressed for office space, Harmonix was forced to move its offices in the middle of <i>Rock Band</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beta_version" title="Beta version">beta period</a> in order to support the company's 130-person staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> However, they continued to bring on more developers in order to complete the title on time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb_postmortem_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-rb_postmortem-42">[42]</a></sup> This led to several problems in bringing the newer coders on board without any technical plan, requiring the team to redesign several parts of the game, such as online matchmaking, several times to correct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb_postmortem_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-rb_postmortem-42">[42]</a></sup> Although the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions of the game were developed in-house, Harmonix outsourced development of the PlayStation 2 version to <a href="/wiki/Pi_Studios" title="Pi Studios">Pi Studios</a>, as it omits certain features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbps_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbps-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harmonix faced difficulty in making the Xbox 360 guitar wireless, as developers are charged a licensing fee to use Microsoft's wireless technology. Had Harmonix chosen to pay the fee, the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 bundles of <i>Rock Band</i> would have sold at different price points. Instead, Harmonix chose a wired technology for the Xbox 360 bundle's guitar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbps_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbps-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Rock Band</i> was first announced on April 1, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today-39">[39]</a></sup> Harmonix CEO Alex Rigopulos said in the announcement that <i>Rock Band</i> "takes the core premise of <i>Guitar Hero</i> and expands it tenfold. It lets you create a complete collaborative band."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today-39">[39]</a></sup> <i>Rock Band</i> was a featured game at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">E3</a> convention and provided one of the exhibition's highlights; Harmonix employees and Microsoft executive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Moore_(business)" title="Peter Moore (business)">Peter Moore</a> played the game on-stage, performing <a href="/wiki/The_Hives" title="The Hives">The Hives</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Main_Offender_(song)" title="Main Offender (song)">Main Offender</a>". Moore paused the game twice when he accidentally hit the guitar's Xbox Guide button.</p>
<p>A software update was released on March 21, 2008, which added new features to the game. The update included an in-game music store with preview and sorting options, revised microphone performance, and faster downloadable content loading.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_community">Online community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Online community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 25, 2007, Harmonix and MTV announced <a class="external text" href="http://www.rockband.com/" rel="nofollow">RockBand.com</a> would be transformed into an extensive community website at the game's launch, and that it would extend the features of the game. The community website was absent at the game's launch in order to fix bugs and complete features, but was launched on December 19, 2007. The site offered leaderboards, customizable band profile pages with stats, a classified area for bands to find additional members, band blogs, online forums, and other sharing features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Many originally announced features, such as the ability for players to pose their avatars, take photo shoots and order T-shirts, bumper stickers, and figurines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alex-oxm_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-alex-oxm-28">[28]</a></sup> were eventually made available on the website for <i>Rock Band 2</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MTV and Harmonix promoted <i>Rock Band</i> heavily in the months leading up to the game's release. The game made a nationwide promotional tour of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-tour_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-rb-tour-46">[46]</a></sup> Several tour buses made stops at major American cities to set up demo stations and showcase playable versions of the game for fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-tour_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-rb-tour-46">[46]</a></sup> Many of the locations included college campuses. Additionally, fan-created "bands" were able to audition on-stage by playing the game; their performances were recorded and sent to MTV casting directors, who selected two bands to appear on <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a></i> in a "battle of the bands." The promotional tour commenced with a featured showcase at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a> on September 9, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb-tour_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-rb-tour-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>MTV invested in additional promotions that totaled about $30 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-47">[47]</a></sup> The game was set up within the homes of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Real_World" title="The Real World">The Real World</a></i> participants, allowing for on-air visibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> also produced a brief spoof documentary in the style of <i><a href="/wiki/Behind_the_Music" title="Behind the Music">Behind the Music</a></i> titled "<i>Rock Band</i> Cometh: The <i>Rock Band</i> Band Story," documenting a fictional band that plays the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game appeared in demo <a href="/wiki/Interactive_kiosk" title="Interactive kiosk">kiosks</a> at <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a> stores. The demo contained 15 songs and supports gameplay for all 4 instruments (although the actual in-store setup varied). The demo's drum set lacked a bass pedal, with the game automatically playing bass drum notes.</p>
<p>Other companies helped to promote <i>Rock Band</i> through free and reduced cost downloadable content. <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a> offered two free downloadable tracks by the band <a href="/wiki/Disturbed_(band)" title="Disturbed (band)">Disturbed</a> for customers that pre-ordered their <i><a href="/wiki/Indestructible_(Disturbed_album)" title="Indestructible (Disturbed album)">Indestructible</a></i> album online; these tracks were made available to all users in June 2008 for $0.99/80MSP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> sponsored a month-long program that reduced the cost of two selected downloadable tracks to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">$</a>1 (approximately half the standard cost) for each week during the month of May 2008 as part of their Dollar Menu promotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United Kingdom release of the game took place in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, where a number of bands including <a href="/wiki/The_Automatic" title="The Automatic">The Automatic</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Whip_(band)" title="The Whip (band)">The Whip</a>, and The Courteeners performed short sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editions">Editions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Editions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div style="font-size:90%;float:right;border-left:1em solid white;">

<p>The "Special Edition" bundle includes the game software, as well as guitar, drum, and microphone peripherals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bundle-SKU_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-bundle-SKU-51">[51]</a></sup> The PlayStation 2, PlayStation 3, and Wii bundles include a wireless guitar, whereas the Xbox 360 bundle contains a wired guitar (a separate wireless guitar is currently available for the Xbox 360). Initially, a <a href="/wiki/USB_hub" title="USB hub">USB hub</a> was only included in the Xbox 360, Wii, and PlayStation 2 bundles, in order to increase the number of available USB ports on the console. The more recent PlayStation 3 bundles now include a USB hub, with a sticker on the box indicating so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> MTV originally announced <i>Rock Band</i> would be released for the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 on November 23, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Black_Friday_(shopping)" title="Black Friday (shopping)">Black Friday</a>, one of the busiest shopping days in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bundle-SKU_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-bundle-SKU-51">[51]</a></sup> However, the release date was eventually moved to November 20, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespy-preview_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-gamespy-preview-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game software was made available for purchase individually at the game's launch,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-169price_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-169price-53">[53]</a></sup> allowing players with a USB microphone or a compatible guitar controller to take advantage of the vocals, lead guitar, and bass guitar gameplay. Individual <i>Rock Band</i>-branded instruments became available in retail stores later, starting with the drum kit on February 12, 2008. An individual wireless guitar became available on April 8, 2008.</p>
<p>On April 8, 2008, EA announced a timed Xbox 360 exclusive for a partial European launch, with other versions to follow later in the summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-may23_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-may23-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_issues_and_guitar_incompatibility">Technical issues and guitar incompatibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Technical issues and guitar incompatibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG/200px-RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG/300px-RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG/400px-RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RB_Pedal_Broken.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A snapped bass drum pedal. This is one common malfunction occurring in <i>Rock Band</i> peripherals</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon release, many players reported hardware issues with <i>Rock Band</i> peripherals. Many complaints stemmed from the bass drum pedal snapping in two, the Stratocaster controller's strum bar being unresponsive, and it occasionally lagging when tilted to activate Overdrive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In response to these issues, Harmonix admitted the guitars bundled with initial shipment of the game bundles were subject to manufacturing issues and stated that they would replace all faulty peripherals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Players affected by faulty peripherals were able to take advantage of the 60-day warranty on the peripherals and obtain replacements from EA. However, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_action_lawsuit" title="Class action lawsuit">class action lawsuit</a> was issued against Harmonix, MTV Games, Viacom, and Electronic Arts over the failures of the bass drum pedal, claiming the companies conspired to force consumers to pay for repairs or upgrade to the <i>Rock Band 2</i> drum kit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Attempts were made to settle the lawsuit in 2008, but were unsuccessful. In September 2009, the original plaintiff dropped the lawsuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other players discovered at the game's launch that the <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul" title="Gibson Les Paul">Gibson Les Paul</a> guitar controller bundled with the PlayStation 3 version of <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_III:_Legends_of_Rock" title="Guitar Hero III: Legends of Rock">Guitar Hero III: Legends of Rock</a></i> was initially not compatible with the PlayStation 3 version of <i>Rock Band</i>, despite Harmonix stating that any controllers that followed the open-controller standard would work. While this incompatibility could have been resolved through technical solutions, both Harmonix and Activision cited the other party as being at fault for failing to correct the incompatibility. Harmonix developed a patch to fix the issue, but it was blocked by Activision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Activision stated that MTV Games was unwilling to reach an agreement to pay Activision to use the <i>Guitar Hero III</i> technology in <i>Rock Band</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> This incompatibility also applies to the Wii's Les Paul peripheral. However, a patch for the PlayStation 3 version of <i>Rock Band</i> was eventually released on September 11, 2008, allowing the <i>Guitar Hero III</i> Les Paul controller to work with <i>Rock Band</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nyko" title="Nyko">Nyko</a> has released a PlayStation 3 version of their "Frontman" guitar controller that is compatible with both <i>Guitar Hero III</i> and <i>Rock Band</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>At a press conference at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">E3</a> convention, Activision confirmed that the Xbox 360 version of <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_World_Tour" title="Guitar Hero World Tour">Guitar Hero World Tour</a></i> will be able to use <i>Rock Band</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s instruments, adapting the note tracks to account for the smaller number of drum pads, and that this compatibility was patched into <i>Guitar Hero: Aerosmith</i> as a result of additional arrangements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired_rb_instruments_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-wired_rb_instruments-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%; width:40%; float:right; text-align:center; margin:5px;">
<tr>
<th colspan="3" style="background:#ccf; font-size:110%;">Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="background:#dde;">Publication</th>
<th style="background:#dde;">Score</th>
<th style="background:#dde;">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/1UP.com" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a></td>
<td>A<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up-review_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-1up-review-65">[65]</a></sup></td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Gaming_Monthly" title="Electronic Gaming Monthly">Electronic Gaming Monthly</a></i></td>
<td>9.0, 9.5, 9.0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></td>
<td>Gold Award</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i></td>
<td>9.25/10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GI-review_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-GI-review-67">[67]</a></sup></td>
<td></td>
</tr>

<p>Prior to release, EA CEO John Riccitielo remarked that the company would not be able to meet the high demand for <i>Rock Band</i> in the 2007 holiday season, stating, "We're not going to be able to put enough inventory to meet demand in North America or Europe this calendar year or this fiscal [year]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> This prompted many retailers to limit the number of preorders they sold before the game was released.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Official_Xbox_Magazine" title="Official Xbox Magazine">Official Xbox Magazine</a></i> published the first review of <i>Rock Band</i>, scoring the Xbox 360 version a 9.5/10 and calling it "gaming's most intensely rewarding co-op experience." <i>OXM</i> also commented that the game's "payoff isn't visceral or technical; it's emotional."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxm-review_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-oxm-review-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> awarded the game a 9.4/10 score and an Editor's Choice Award for the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions. IGN largely praised the game, calling it "one of the must-have games of the year" and suggesting it "may just be among the best party games ever released."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-review_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign-review-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1UP.com" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a> gave the next-generation versions of the game an A,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up-review_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-1up-review-65">[65]</a></sup> stating that "<i>Rock Band</i> unquestionably, unequivocally rocks." <a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a> rated the next-generation versions of the game a 9.0/10, calling <i>Rock Band</i> "one of the best party games of all time." They also gave the game their Editor's Choice award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-review_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-review-69">[69]</a></sup> The Xbox 360 version of <i>Rock Band</i> has an average critic score of 92%, according to <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, tying it for the 24th-highest-scored Xbox 360 game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic-360_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-360-101">[101]</a></sup> Similarly, the PlayStation 3 version of <i>Rock Band</i> has an average critic score of 92% on Metacritic, making it the 25th-highest-scored PlayStation 3 game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic-ps3_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-ps3-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most critics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up-review_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-1up-review-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GI-review_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-GI-review-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-review_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-review-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-review_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-ign-review-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxm-review_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-oxm-review-71">[71]</a></sup> have commended the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3 versions of <i>Rock Band</i> for the game's group gameplay, the depth of Band World Tour mode, and the introduction of a drum peripheral. Common complaints about the game focus on the different feel of the packaged Fender Stratocaster controller,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GI-review_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-GI-review-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-review_70-3"><a href="#cite_note-ign-review-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxm-review_71-3"><a href="#cite_note-oxm-review-71">[71]</a></sup> as well as the game's Solo Tour modes not being as enjoyable as the multiplayer offerings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up-review_65-3"><a href="#cite_note-1up-review-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-review_70-4"><a href="#cite_note-ign-review-70">[70]</a></sup> IGN's video review lamented the lack of a single player Band World Tour mode.</p>
<p>The PlayStation 2 version of the game was well received, but was subject to criticism for the omission of the character customization features, as well as the stripped-down Band World Tour mode. GameSpot rated it an 8.0/10, stating that "<i>Rock Band</i> is still a lot of fun on the PS2—it's just nowhere near the ideal version of the experience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot-review-ps2_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot-review-ps2-94">[94]</a></sup> IGN.com rated it an 8.4/10, noting that the removed features made the game feel like a "lessened" version, but that the game still "succeeds because it's infinitely fun to play with your friends."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-review-ps2_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign-review-ps2-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Reviews for the Wii version of <i>Rock Band</i> also criticize the lack of features compared to the PlayStation 3 and Xbox 360 versions. The Wii version is basically the same as its PlayStation 2 counterpart, but IGN criticized it for its late release and their effort in completing a full game. However, IGN noted that the drum controller is an improvement over the original version, stating, "The pads are quieter and the kick pedal will withstand more abuse."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-review-wii_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign-review-wii-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales">Sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By October 9, 2008, the game sold four million units and generated global revenues of $600 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-salesfigure_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-salesfigure-9">[9]</a></sup> The sales of <i>Rock Band</i> helped <a href="/wiki/Viacom" title="Viacom">Viacom</a> to become the fifth-largest video game publisher in the United States, although analysts estimated that Viacom was only breaking even on sales of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dow_jones_sales_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-dow_jones_sales-103">[103]</a></sup> In a March 2011 list, the NPD Group listed <i>Rock Band</i> as the fifth-highest-grossing video game in the United States since 1995, earning $670.7 million in revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>By May 2011, over 100 million songs had been downloaded from the <i>Rock Band</i> music store.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-may2011_dlc_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-may2011_dlc-10">[10]</a></sup> Viacom estimated that it is averaging the sale of 1 million downloadable songs every 9 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dow_jones_sales_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-dow_jones_sales-103">[103]</a></sup> Sales of songs were in favor of hard rock bands; <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe" title="Mötley Crüe">Mötley Crüe</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s single "Saints of Los Angeles", debuting as a <i>Rock Band</i> track at the same time as the release of the album of the same name, saw 48,000 <i>Rock Band</i> downloads and 14,000 <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> downloads during its first week of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_rb2_gnr_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_rb2_gnr-105">[105]</a></sup> The popularity of some tracks also led to groups considering releasing more material for the game. <a href="/wiki/Rush_(band)" title="Rush (band)">Rush</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s alternate version of "<a href="/wiki/Working_Man" title="Working Man">Working Man</a>" released only for <i>Rock Band</i> was met with so much praise from players of <i>Rock Band</i> that the group released the song for download through <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>, as well as considered making full albums available,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_rb2_gnr_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_rb2_gnr-105">[105]</a></sup> which they went on to do for their 1981 album <i><a href="/wiki/Moving_Pictures_(Rush_album)" title="Moving Pictures (Rush album)">Moving Pictures</a></i>, released for the game two months later.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to the game's release, <i>Rock Band</i> was featured at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_E3#2007_.28July_11.E2.80.9313.29" title="History of E3">2007 E3 convention</a>, garnering attention and several awards, including the Game Critics' "Best of E3 2007" awards for "Best of Show," "Best Hardware/Peripheral," and "Best Social/Casual/Puzzle,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> 1UP.com's "Best of E3,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and GameSpot's "Best Stage Demo"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> and "Best Xbox 360 Game."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>After its release, <i>Rock Band</i> won dozens of awards covering game releases from 2007. The game won seven awards from IGN's "Best of 2007," receiving honors for "Best Music Game" for the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07a_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07a-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07aa_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07aa-82">[82]</a></sup> "Best Local Multiplayer Game" for the Xbox 360 and PlayStation 3,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07b_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07b-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07bb_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07bb-84">[84]</a></sup> "Best Downloadable Content" for the PlayStation 3,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07c_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07c-85">[85]</a></sup> and "Best Console Peripheral,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07d_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07d-86">[86]</a></sup> as well as overall awards for "Best Music Game,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07e_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07e-87">[87]</a></sup> "Best Licensed Soundtrack,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07f_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07f-88">[88]</a></sup> and "Best Local Multiplayer Game."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign07g_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign07g-89">[89]</a></sup> GameSpot awarded <i>Rock Band</i> five awards in its "Best of 2007," recognizing the game for "Best Rhythm/Music Game,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gs07a_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-gs07a-76">[76]</a></sup> "Best New Gaming Hardware,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gs07b_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-gs07b-77">[77]</a></sup> "Best Downloadable Content,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gs07c_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-gs07c-78">[78]</a></sup> "Best Sound Design,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gs07d_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-gs07d-79">[79]</a></sup> and "Best Multiplayer Game."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gs07e_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-gs07e-80">[80]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-wired-92">[92]</a></sup> <i>Official Xbox Magazine</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxm07_90-3"><a href="#cite_note-oxm07-90">[90]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> all named <i>Rock Band</i> the "Game of the Year," while <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Next_Generation_Magazine" title="Next Generation Magazine">Next Generation Magazine</a></i> named it the second-best game of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GamePro" title="GamePro">GamePro</a> honored <i>Rock Band</i> with the "Innovation Award" for four-person cooperative play,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gp07a_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-gp07a-74">[74]</a></sup> as well as the selection of "Best Party Game" of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gp07b_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-gp07b-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GameSpy" title="GameSpy">GameSpy</a> also recognized the game as the "Music Game of the Year" on the Xbox 360<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> and PlayStation 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Additionally, <i>Rock Band</i> was awarded "Best Multiplayer Experience (console)" by 1UP.com.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up07_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-1up07-73">[73]</a></sup> The game won two awards at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Spike_Video_Game_Awards" title="Spike Video Game Awards">Spike Video Game Awards</a>, receiving honors for "Best Rhythm Game" and "Best Soundtrack," while the game's developer, Harmonix, won "Studio of the Year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spikevga_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-spikevga-91">[91]</a></sup> The game also won an award for "Best Multiplayer Game" in the <i><a href="/wiki/X-Play" title="X-Play">X-Play</a></i> Best of 2007 Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_of_Interactive_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Academy of Interactive Arts and Sciences">Academy of Interactive Arts and Sciences</a> awarded <i>Rock Band</i> with honors for three of the eight categories in which it was nominated; the game won awards for "Family Game of the Year", "Outstanding Achievement in Soundtrack", and "Outstanding Innovation in Gaming".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> <i>Rock Band</i> was named "Best Party Game" of the year from <i>Game Informer Magazine</i>. The game has also been called the best rhythm game of all time by <a href="/wiki/GameTap" title="GameTap">GameTap</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_impact">Cultural impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cultural impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rock_Band#Cultural_impact" title="Rock Band">Cultural impact of Rock Band series</a></div>
<p>Like the <a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero"><i>Guitar Hero</i> series</a>, <i>Rock Band</i> has had a significant impact on culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_rb2_gnr_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_rb2_gnr-105">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rigopulos" title="Alex Rigopulos">Alex Rigopulos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eran_Egozy" title="Eran Egozy">Eran Egozy</a>, the founders of Harmonix, were together named in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" title="Time Magazine">Time Magazine</a>'</i>s list of the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100 most influential people</a> of 2008 for their creation of <i>Rock Band</i>. In the article, guitarist <a href="/wiki/Steven_Van_Zandt" title="Steven Van Zandt">Steven Van Zandt</a> claims, "in the history of <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock 'n' roll</a>, <i>Rock Band</i> may just turn out to be up there with the rise of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FM_radio" title="FM radio">FM radio</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compact_Disc" title="Compact Disc">CDs</a>, or <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequel">Sequel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sequel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_2" title="Rock Band 2">Rock Band 2</a></div>
<p><i>Rock Band 2</i> was officially announced on June 30, 2008, and was released on September 14, 2008 on the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, with other platform releases following later in the year. Original instruments from <i>Rock Band</i> are compatible with <i>Rock Band 2</i>, which features new instruments that been described as quieter and more reliable. Furthermore, both existing and any forthcoming downloadable content will be cross-compatible between <i>Rock Band</i> and <i>Rock Band 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb2_ign_announce_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-rb2_ign_announce-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rb2_ign_opening_act_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-rb2_ign_opening_act-119">[119]</a></sup> <i>Rock Band 2</i> saw enhancements to the existing Band World Tour mode, as well as inclusions of new "Drum Trainer" and "Battle of the Bands" modes. 55 of the 58 <i>Rock Band</i> songs can be exported for use in <i>Rock Band 2</i>, with the purchase of a $5 export key.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Patent_litigation">Patent litigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rock_Band_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Patent litigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 21, 2008, EA, MTV, and Harmonix were sued by the <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation" title="Gibson Guitar Corporation">Gibson Guitar Corporation</a> for violation of the 1999 <span><a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US5990405" rel="nofollow">U.S. Patent 5,990,405</a></span>, which Gibson claims covers technology that simulates a concert performance via pre-recorded audio and a musical instrument; this follows similar action that Gibson has taken against the <i>Guitar Hero</i> series, which was later settled out of court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The Gibson-Harmonix case was put on hold shortly after its filing to allow the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> to open a re-examination of the 405 patent. On subsequent review, the 405 patent was modified to more exactly define the type of musical instrument that the patent covers, as the original language had conflicted with <span><a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US5488196" rel="nofollow">U.S. Patent 5,488,196</a></span>. Due to the change in language, Harmonix sought to have the case go forward and requested a summary judgement, believing that the new language of the 405 patent did not include the <i>Rock Band</i> controllers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In mid 2010, the case was settled between all parties under non-disclosed terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 10, 2008, <a href="/wiki/Konami" title="Konami">Konami</a> filed a separate lawsuit against Harmonix, <a href="/wiki/Viacom" title="Viacom">Viacom</a>, and MTV attempting to block the sale of <i>Rock Band</i>, over infringement of their patents on a "musical-rhythm matching game" issued in 2002 and 2003, including <span><a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US6390923" rel="nofollow">U.S. Patent 6,390,923</a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> An MTV spokesperson expressed that the lawsuit was "extremely surprising" and that they intend to defend themselves against the suit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> On December 2, 2008, Viacom issued a countersuit against Konami, claiming that <i>Rock Band</i> significantly improves on Konami's original patent, and that their <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Revolution" title="Rock Revolution">Rock Revolution</a></i> game uses controllers that are similar to <i>Rock Band</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Both suits were settled for undisclosed terms in September 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
